This is where the NFS layer callback would be invoked to process the result. So even if ERESTARTSYS is set, the callback is still called.\n\nNow, the key issue is: when rpc_exit is called with -ERESTARTSYS in the signal handler path (from sched.c line 792), has the server's reply already been received and processed? \n\nLooking back at the code in sched.c:\n```c\nif (status == -ERESTARTSYS) {\n    /*\n     * When a sync task receives a signal, it exits with\n     * -ERESTARTSYS. In order to catch any callbacks that\n     * clean up after sleeping on some queue, we don't\n     * break the loop here, but go around once more.\n     */\n    dprintk(\"RPC: %5u got signal\\n\", task->tk_pid);\n    task->tk_flags |= RPC_TASK_KILLED;\n    rpc_exit(task, -ERESTARTSYS);\n}\n```\n\nThis suggests that when a signal interrupts the wait for the reply, the task exits with -ERESTARTSYS even if the reply hasn't been received yet.\n\nBut the bug report says:\n\"tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.\"\n\nThis suggests that the reply is being received, but due to signal handling, it's being treated as an error.\n\nThe real issue might be more subtle. Let me look at what happens when a reply is received after a signal has been sent. Maybe the reply is received but by the time it gets processed, the task has already been marked as killed or exited.\n\nLet me search for where RPC replies are processed. Then line 39 unconditionally sets res = -ERESTARTSYS. This is the bug!\n\nThe return value of freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe indicates whether the sleep was interrupted. If it returns 0, the sleep completed normally. If it returns > 0, it was interrupted and the caller should exit. But the code ignores this and just sets res = -ERESTARTSYS unconditionally!\n\nActually wait, let me think about this more. The check on line 40 is `while (!fatal_signal_pending(current))`. If the sleep returned early due to a signal, we should respect that and NOT continue retrying.\n\n\nHmm, setting res = -ERESTARTSYS unconditionally seems odd. The return value from the sleep should matter—if it completes normally, res should stay -EJUKEBOX to trigger another RPC attempt, not become an error code. Only when a signal actually interrupts should we bail out with an error. The loop condition checks for fatal signals afterward, but by then res has already been overwritten. The timing of when the signal arrives matters—if it comes after the sleep completes but before the fatal_signal_pending check, or if it was already queued, the behavior changes. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01PqzigS4bcwAsMi3awAYXio","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"So the code checks for -ESTALE specifically (line 965), but doesn't have special handling for -ERESTARTSYS. Looking at line 961-970:\n- If status != 0 (any error), print error message\n- If status == -ESTALE, do special handling (zap caches)\n- Otherwise, goto err_out\n\nSo if status == -ERESTARTSYS, it goes to err_out which returns the error (line 995). This error then propagates back to nfs_lookup_verify_inode, which returns it (line 1074-1075 in dir.c):\n\n```c\nret = __nfs_revalidate_inode(server, inode);\nif (ret != 0)\n    return ret;\n```\n\nAnd if nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns a non-zero value, nfs_lookup_revalidate treats it as a failure and goes to out_bad (line 1161 in dir.c), which invalidates the dentry.So the bug is: __nfs_revalidate_inode should handle ERESTARTSYS specially, not treat it as a permanent failure.One approach is to retry when ERESTARTSYS is encountered. Another approach is to not treat ERESTARTSYS as a failure - instead, return 0 (success) to indicate that the dentry should still be valid even if the revalidation was interrupted.Actually, thinking about this more, the real problem is that nfs3_rpc_wrapper unconditionally sets res = -ERESTARTSYS after the sleep, without checking if the sleep was actually interrupted. Let me look at that code again.Actually, I just realized something. Looking back at the nfs3_rpc_wrapper code:```cdo {    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n    if (res != -EJUKEBOX)        break;\n    freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n    res = -ERESTARTSYS;\n} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n```\n\nThe issue is that after the sleep completes, the code sets res = -ERESTARTSYS and then checks if a signal is pending. If no signal occurred, the loop continues and the next rpc_call_sync overwrites that error code anyway, so the intermediate assignment doesn't actually affect the outcome.\n\nHowever, there's a critical problem: when a signal IS detected at the loop condition, the function returns -ERESTARTSYS even though the most recent RPC call might have succeeded. Additionally, there's a race condition where a signal could arrive between the loop condition check and the start of the next iteration, potentially causing the signal to be missed entirely.\n\nLooking at the actual control flow more carefully:\n```\ndo {\n    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);  // Line 35\n    if (res != -EJUKEBOX)                   // Line 36\n        break;                               // Line 37\n    freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);  // Line 38\n    res = -ERESTARTSYS;                      // Line 39\n} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));    // Line 40\n```\n\nWhen a signal arrives during the sleep, the scheduler wakes the process, the code sets res to -ERESTARTSYS, then checks for pending signals and exits the loop. This seems correct on the surface, but the issue is that -ERESTARTSYS gets returned regardless of whether the last RPC attempt actually failed or succeeded.\n\nLet me consider what happens if the signal comes after the sleep completes normally—the code still returns -ERESTARTSYS even though the RPC might have succeeded. The real problem appears to be in how the code handles the interaction between signal delivery and RPC retry logic, particularly in the context of the autofs behavior change between kernel versions.\n\nThe bug report describes an issue where autofs mounts disappear unexpectedly after upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15, specifically on NFS-mounted root filesystems. The problem manifests as both the submount and the parent mount being unmounted during expiration. The NFS layer reports getattr failures with error -512, which causes inode revalidation to fail and triggers unmounting of all mounts on that inode. This suggests the signal handling in the RPC code is causing premature termination of operations that should complete, leading to stale inode state. The reply might arrive after the task has already been interrupted and is exiting, leaving it orphaned. This could explain why tcpdump shows the server responding correctly but the client never processes it.\n\nLooking at nfs3_rpc_wrapper, I notice it specifically checks for -EJUKEBOX returns. But getattr shouldn't typically return EJUKEBOX on a standard NFS mount. More importantly, when getattr is called through nfs_lookup_revalidate via __nfs_revalidate_inode, it bypasses nfs3_rpc_wrapper entirely and calls rpc_call_sync directly. This difference in code paths might be significant—one path has retry logic while the other doesn't.","signature":"EoUzCkYICxgCKkBY1vXngJs2i/6aeY1ZvgcpNIHcTcbfqkOUGX2PwWa7q50xhAN7X4qJocWOtpi/uutbv6fb6H67Mfnu0ic0DknZEgxyWtAPVyeUyTU9KJgaDIuOPztndp1RVM71ZCIwZ13xYwN8kf+mIoMOKeN7G+nt8E6OqBnkokuegeUbWBs8ddrP1XRVtRZ8YG3/Q8ScKuwxHCKz7nK05ACo94GbPxVqDvkP3MexYuBU7eDj2uHLO5FAmDJV2n8jgcQZK8LQZDJIVGs8IJ86aEVpnfXduayO4lPxDQzhS2v2rafs2OgWCK5aiU1OB8DeqdC/3piS4jbqiS6bc5sXdzzFXWagdSHHFG3l+07ofptbPxq0oEIhgsxNMPXnx4JCDhsERaF92z8haHiachFKXsXs+ebRQpM6c1lcVMZfQoZokgmw5SpOMTz3LVOZ2Q4jdq1aBVGxaFZWv9rnQVOr4t4OtTlZcj/xtisy1s0ZQQE/fy/18OujVRJ9ENk3vmea6tOlavI+tL4TFmmlLUbnuwGEb+Rcsv+MHIy6KQf2g6uZdF47Qg3OqpcFWFVIpGgM1wZxyoGtwWL54AT430M9lHJpWMFxBPdhVQYMM8/PRHuNEwlvnRj3Bmt2ERVBZ93EwssNUP4djOEBoXpp9GyUwzgZLss0jBcgJB6iAmbLZ6EI/Bm1J9quAWpfXdT0a6TtFi28t5m8WGKnYlbCKsWGfPeIkK3O0yhVTTjRMmxsarlFMtAWdVcl+z5HX6bO2vw+1zYUoU1a7f0hj6BzLVnjGv0vbOR6Se2Zog8gThkuJKJsuI7JRGX/X2U/j4BKwUgRrcITUBDVf1dFyD2dmwP64ITJOunOt2zAaxCUwMpk+ccweO11Oe4R+DDv/qrHxp+xpp2EHGyuL41/ef511pQq86fJ8bP7rGVfo+KYsfM0/YQsj3pW8ah4cNJnpaCgkm/N9VTl65ak9/MvlQ9Hg11q7N5B7WLSjpe0E8hhU+2pl3Yf+I5ixT64hEblKOu8SusRvTKAWTxxjTffNsyOCfW8hptNUpsKYirj8x6rko21TOdD0fZPFazmPGfh9oa3k7y3mmMYR6itXOvEnPyarwHrUmgn01H1mMhtIszwbP4uckbZnnV/1t39hMVnircqjfHf3B5OLNiPPax44I7xaIBe8FdzBwnCi8lV8fczpl/Y1obkHIkulkQL9B4tOD24Fq1s4eETT8cPNR9r9VWR3T/yeF5VaknaltQHN9aDYR9MRO9WDKuK6/O2/r6FAynhqoSn3LhIUGmGegJiMdad00C3pHJ9DlujlQte4n+941zlGPwsKine9zJUmmbqrzVI4UZO/etPTv8U14A3AULI6MEes3hf/Q+M7ZxIbaOidaEOXSQEccXEjaJADBBMPMAvxCoYPXZ9hR1oxRwtVxVt+2kYLVCDC7O/U/8/YqdjD4S0of66UuRT2ZCKwckvj/crvOrFRw+4aYs7FHHhLAMcfAaXMVR1rUmnEREtUIvUnpAmRUSvuCUZgCiud1xbJJfN/g9Im8Ckj4Vvhc8CSCJfw+d6yp9Q//LcPy2luXGQQXoXPqxzhMZ7WZt17f4YhcbwNsxa7NonCwUx4Dn/l2ytwPTGNBtqwn6cXY4Ctmfa4spUyLiNDdcAs+j30lpObPW0DbGkIDTTpH9LwMpfoXPuiejiwePW+kvmvAb4FWBj9pVeSBPp5lVFMcgrUOKyRFfojH6WbHiDnVQNQkPzWATcK8GT1Ip+hbir+sZlLVn3pe7SR5xfg5aSdzpaamGy4lGbN5ar2NvHSpwtslkAkqI/rz1prAextHBt09h2Hyirv0TeF4JF4OrEq1++W749KSdhxzLsCbyLFVu1NHyX4Iy0Wdg82XsQPXzBTezpdJbcsgbGy5WnguxOb1pnkXgP59tnkBIRhSZ35wAa+Iulz0ewWO6O9jIA3K00iw4Zum6e6oRGOj8ftATVlStl6 {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01N6uGvyXtJqbgFbHApV3fzS","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Good, the result file is created. But let me double-check my analysis by looking more carefully at the nfs3_rpc_wrapper code. Maybe I'm missing something and the actual bug is elsewhere.\n\nLet me reconsider. The error messages in the bug report are:\n- \"NFS reply getattr: -512\"\n- \"nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512\"\n- \"NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid\"\n\nThis suggests that:\n1. getattr (nfs3_proc_getattr) is returning -512\n2. __nfs_revalidate_inode is seeing this error\n3. nfs_lookup_revalidate is invalidating the dentry\n\nThe -512 is ERESTARTSYS. So the question is: why is nfs3_proc_getattr returning -512?\n\nLet me trace the code path:\n1. nfs3_proc_getattr calls rpc_call_sync (which is now nfs3_rpc_wrapper due to #define)\n2. nfs3_rpc_wrapper calls rpc_call_sync (the real one)\n3. rpc_call_sync might return -ERESTARTSYS if a signal interrupts the RPC\n\nSo the question is: why would rpc_call_sync return -ERESTARTSYS?\n\nLooking at the RPC layer code I examined earlier:\n- In sched.c, when a sync task receives a signal while waiting, rpc_exit is called with -ERESTARTSYS\n- This causes the task to exit with that error\n\nSo the flow could be:\n1. nfs3_proc_getattr calls rpc_call_sync (wrapper)\n2. Wrapper calls real rpc_call_sync\n3. Real rpc_call_sync makes an RPC call\n4. Task waits for reply\n5. Signal is sent to the task\n\n\n6. Task wakes with -ERESTARTSYS and the wrapper receives this error code instead of -EJUKEBOX, so it breaks out of the loop and returns the error directly. This propagates back through nfs3_proc_getattr to __nfs_revalidate_inode, which passes it to nfs_lookup_revalidate. The lookup code then treats this as a validation failure and invalidates the dentry.\n\nThe actual problem might be elsewhere—the signal could be interrupting the initial rpc_call_sync rather than one that returned -EJUKEBOX. If that's the case, __nfs_revalidate_inode needs to handle -ERESTARTSYS by retrying instead of treating it as a permanent failure. Looking at the nfs3proc.c wrapper logic, the loop only continues when res equals -EJUKEBOX, so any other error—including -ERESTARTSYS—causes an immediate exit and return.\n\nThis means the -ERESTARTSYS in the bug report is coming directly from that first rpc_call_sync, not from the JUKEBOX retry mechanism. The real issue is why the initial call returns -ERESTARTSYS and why this worked before the regression.\n\nThe possibilities span several layers: the RPC layer's signal handling could have changed, the NFS layer's RPC invocation might differ, signal handling itself could have shifted, or error propagation could work differently. Another angle is that autofs or the kernel might be sending signals more aggressively in 4.1.15, and the code isn't handling them properly. But the tcpdump evidence is telling—the server sends a valid getattr reply, yet the client either doesn't receive it or fails to process it, suggesting the RPC task itself is being terminated or marked as RPC_TASK before the response arrives.\n\nI suspect a race condition: the getattr call triggers a signal, the task begins exiting with -ERESTARTSYS, but simultaneously the server's reply comes back. The task is already marked as killed, so the reply gets dropped or the error takes precedence. This points to a synchronization issue between signal handling and reply processing in the RPC layer, possibly in nfs3_rpc_wrapper itself.\n\nLooking more carefully at nfs3_rpc_wrapper though—the code at line 39 that sets res = -ERESTARTSYS only executes if the first rpc_call_sync returns -EJUKEBOX. If it returns a different error, the loop breaks and that error is returned instead. So the problematic code path requires -EJUKEBOX to be returned initially, then the sleep completes, and -ERESTARTSYS gets set unconditionally. That sequence would cause getattr to fail with -ERESTARTSYS rather than retrying properly.\n\nThe actual control flow appears to be: the do-while loop calls rpc_call_sync, checks if the result is -EJUKEBOX, and if not, breaks out. When -EJUKEBOX is returned, it calls freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe and sets res = -ERESTARTSYS. The while condition then checks for fatal signals—if none are pending, the loop continues and the next rpc_call_sync call would overwrite res. But there's a potential race: if a signal arrives between the signal check and the next rpc_call_sync, res remains -ERESTARTSYS and the loop breaks on the next iteration when the while condition is re-evaluated. I'm overcomplicating this. The core issue in nfs3_rpc_wrapper is that it sets res = -ERESTARTSYS after the sleep unconditionally, without verifying the sleep was actually interrupted. This behavior seems problematic. The real problem might also be in __nfs_revalidate_inode, which doesn't handle -ERESTARTSYS distinctly—it lumps all non-ESTALE errors together as permanent failures. A fix would involve either retrying the getattr when encountering -ERESTARTSYS, or preventing it from being treated as a fatal error. Looking at the call chain: nfs_lookup_verify_inode invokes __nfs_revalidate_inode, and if that returns an error, nfs_lookup_verify_inode propagates it, causing nfs_lookup_revalidate to mark the dentry invalid. The most sensible fix is probably in nfs_lookup_verify_inode—it should handle transient errors like -ERESTARTSYS differently rather than treating them as validation {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016XtoZzxJGz51DdCSZXNbNU","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"I see. So nfs_lookup_verify_inode at lines 1073-1075 calls __nfs_revalidate_inode and if it returns any non-zero value, it returns that error. So if __nfs_revalidate_inode returns -ERESTARTSYS, then nfs_lookup_verify_inode returns -ERESTARTSYS, which causes nfs_lookup_revalidate to treat the dentry as invalid.\n\nThe problem is that -ERESTARTSYS should not cause dentry invalidation. It's a transient error that means the operation was interrupted by a signal. The inode itself may still be valid.\n\nSo the fix should be: in nfs_lookup_verify_inode, if __nfs_revalidate_inode returns -ERESTARTSYS, it should be treated as if the revalidation didn't happen (i.e., the inode validity should be preserved, not invalidated).\n\nOr alternatively, in __nfs_revalidate_inode, when getattr returns -ERESTARTSYS, it should retry instead of immediately returning the error.\n\nActually, I think the most appropriate fix is to handle -ERESTARTSYS specially as a transient/non-fatal error. When __nfs_revalidate_inode encounters ERESTARTSYS from getattr, it should NOT zap caches and should NOT permanently mark the inode as stale. Instead, it should either:\n1. Return 0 (success) and leave the inode as-is\n2. Retry the getattr\n3. Return ERESTARTSYS but in a way that tells the caller to not invalidate the dentry\n\nLet me look at what the best approach would be. Looking at the code, when __nfs_revalidate_inode encounters -ESTALE, it calls nfs_zap_caches to invalidate the inode. But for -ERESTARTSYS, we don't want to invalidate the inode - we just want to leave it as-is.\n\n\nThe most sensible approach is probably to treat -ERESTARTSYS as a successful revalidation by returning 0, since the inode attributes haven't actually been invalidated—we simply couldn't refresh them due to signal interruption. Alternatively, retrying the revalidation when encountering this transient error might be more {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_015hc8HU1qXhYH9X8DcDwG6g","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Actually, thinking about this more, I'm not entirely confident that both functions need to be fixed. Let me reconsider where the most direct fix would be.\n\nLooking at the code flow:1. __nfs_revalidate_inode calls getattr via NFS_PROTO(inode)->getattr at line 960 in inode.c\n2. If getattr returns -ERESTARTSYS, __nfs_revalidate_inode returns it at line 970\n3. nfs_lookup_verify_inode gets this error and returns it at line 1075\n4. nfs_lookup_revalidate gets this error and treats the dentry as invalid\n\nThe most direct fix would be in __nfs_revalidate_inode to handle -ERESTARTSYS specially. When getattr returns -ERESTARTSYS, __nfs_revalidate_inode could:\n1. Retry the getattr (recommended)\n2. Return 0 (treat as success, don't refresh but don't invalidate)\n3. Return some other indication that this is a transient error\n\nActually, thinking about it more, the best fix is probably to check for -ERESTARTSYS at line 1074-1075 in nfs_lookup_verify_inode, because this is where the decision is made whether to treat an error as \"validation failed\". For transient errors like -ERESTARTSYS, we should not treat them as validation failures.\n\nBut actually, the MOST direct place to fix this is probably in __nfs_revalidate_inode, because that's where we know the revalidation was interrupted by a signal rather than a permanent error.\n\nLet me think about what the minimal fix would be. Looking at line 965-969 in inode.c:\n```cif (status == -ESTALE) {    nfs_zap_caches(inode);    if (!S_ISDIR(inode->i_mode))        set_bit(NFS_INO_STALE, &NFS_I(inode)->flags);\n\n\n}```\n\nThis is special handling for -ESTALE. We could add similar handling for -ERESTARTSYS to NOT do special cache zapping. In fact, we might want to return 0 (success) instead of returning the error, because the inode cache hasn't been invalidated by the operation failure - the operation was just interrupted. Looking at the error handling structure more carefully, when status is non-zero, the code performs special cache invalidation for -ESTALE before jumping to err_out. For -ERESTARTSYS, we should skip that cache zapping since the error is transient and the cached state remains valid.\n\nThe real issue is that both error types currently reach err_out and propagate the error back. For transient interruptions, returning 0 makes more sense—the cached attributes are still good, and the caller can proceed without forcing a revalidation. This differs from -ESTALE where the cache must be cleared because the file handle is genuinely
